# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox DOM Event Dispatch Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a DOM event (e.g., click) is dispatched through the Firefox event system in mozilla/gecko-dev. Find C++ source files implementing: the event creation, the event target identification, the capture/bubble phase traversal, the event listener invocation, and the default action execution.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/firefox--871325b8.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)


55-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully traced the Firefox DOM event dispatch chain and created a comprehensive answer file. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

The Firefox event dispatch system consists of several critical components:

1. **Event Creation** (`EventDispatcher::DispatchDOMEvent` & `::Dispatch`): Initiates event processing and validates security context

2. **Event Target Chain Building** (EventDispatcher.cpp lines 1008-1178): Constructs an ancestor chain by repeatedly calling `GetEventTargetParent()` on each target up the DOM tree

3. **Capture/Bubble/Target Phase Traversal** (`EventTargetChainItem::HandleEventTargetChain`):
   - **Capture Phase**: Iterates backward through chain (root to target)
   - **Target Phase**: Processes the original target
   - **Bubble Phase**: Iterates forward through chain (target to root)
   - Each phase can be stopped via `stopPropagation()`

4. **Event Listener Invocation** (`EventListenerManager::HandleEventInternal` & `HandleEventWithListenerArray`):
   - Retrieves registered listeners by event type
   - Filters listeners by phase (capture vs bubble)
   - Invokes each matching listener callback
   - Handles passive listeners and `once` listeners

5. **Default Action Execution** (`PostHandleEvent` methods):
   - Executed after dispatch if not prevented
   - Implemented in specific event target classes (e.g., HTMLButtonElement)

The answer file at `/workspace/answer.json` contains complete file references, symbol locations with line numbers, the call chain sequence, and a detailed narrative explaining how each component works together to implement the W3C DOM Event specification in Firefox.

well-defined pipeline that creates an event target chain, traverses it through capture/target/bubble phases, and invokes registered event listeners. This implementation follows the W3C DOM Event specification.\\n\\n### Event Creation (dom/events/EventDispatcher.h:27-51, EventDispatcher.cpp)\\n\\nThe event creation and dispatch process begins with `EventDispatcher::DispatchDOMEvent()` (EventDispatcher.cpp:1380) or `EventDispatcher::Dispatch()` (EventDispatcher.cpp:869). i > firstCanHandleEventTargetIdx; --i)`\\n- Calls `item.HandleEvent(aVisitor, aCd)` for each item if propagation is not stopped\\n- Handles event retargeting for touch targets and related targets\\n\\n**Target Phase** (lines 587-611):\\n- Sets `mEvent->mFlags.mInTargetPhase = true`\\n- Calls `HandleEvent()` twice: once for capture listeners, once for bubble listeners\\n- The second call sets `mEvent->mFlags.mInBubblingPhase = true` to allow bubble-phase listeners\\n\\n**Bubble Phase** (lines 613-648):\\n- Sets `mEvent->mFlags.mInBubblingPhase = true`, `mInCapturePhase = false`\\n- Iterates the chain **forward** (from target to root): `for (uint32_t i = firstCanHandleEventTargetIdx + 1; i < chainLength; ++i)`\\n- Only processes events where `mEvent->mFlags.mBubbles` is true\\n- Calls `item.HandleEvent()` and `PostHandleEvent()` for each ancestor\\n\\n**System Group Dispatch** (lines 651-693):\\n- If the event can be dispatched in the system event group, repeats capture/target/bubble phases\\n- System group listeners are called after the default event group\\n\\n### Event Listener Invocation (EventListenerManager.cpp)\\n\\nWhen `EventTargetChainItem::HandleEvent()` is called (EventDispatcher.cpp:339-370):\\n1. Calls `HandleEventWithListenerArray()` for all-event listeners\\n   - Calls `HandleEventWithListenerArray()` for type-specific listeners\\n   - Handles legacy event versions (e.g., `dblclick` for phase (capture vs bubble)\\n     - Verifies the event trustedness is acceptable\\n     - Handles `once` listeners by moving them to the stack before invocation\\n     - Calls listener state via `mInPassiveListener` flag\\n   - Sets the window event if on the main thread\\n   - Invokes the listener callback (JavaScript function or native handler)\\n   - Stores the passive flag state for preventDefault() validation\\n\\n### Default Action Execution (PostHandleEvent methods)\\n\\nDefault actions are executed after event dispatch through the `PostHandleEvent()` mechanism:\\n- Called for each item in the chain during system group dispatch\\n- Defined in specific event target implementations (e.g., `HTMLButtonElement::PostHandleEvent()`)\\n- Can be prevented by calling `preventDefault()` if the event is `cancelable`\\n- Examples include form submission for button clicks, navigation for link clicks\\n\\n### Key Data Structures\\n\\n**EventChainPreVisitor** (EventDispatcher.h:113-310):\\n- Maintains event state during chain building\\n- Tracks retargeting information for shadow DOM and anonymous content\\n- Controls whether items handle the event (`mCanHandle`)\\n\\n**EventChainPostVisitor** (EventDispatcher.h:312-323):\\n- Used during event dispatch phase\\n- Carries event status and dispatch results\\n\\n**EventTargetChainItem** (EventDispatcher.cpp:102-427):\\n- Represents a single node in the event target chain\\n- Caches listener manager and event target info\\n- Handles event propagation through phases\\n\\n### Flags Controlling Dispatch\\n\\nWidgetEvent.mFlags controls dispatch behavior (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp and BasicEvents.h):\\n- `mInCapturePhase`: Currently in capture phase\\n- `mInBubblingPhase`: Currently in bubble phase\\n- `mInTargetPhase`: Currently at target\\n- `mBubbles`: Event can bubble to ancestors\\n- `mCancelable`: Event can be cancelled with preventDefault()\\n-
